  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dcc03e68-d305-4a2a-a476-79852c3ca616'

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_490').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16456751081943995908">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I picked up Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Reading the synopsis really didn’t prepare me for how intense this book really is! I’m still not sure how to classify it, but I will say that I now have a better grasp of dark fiction as a genre... sub genre?<br/><br/>The beginning has this hook- a woman’s nightmare - this violent crime against her spirals into a mother’s worst fear that her son has completely gone over the edge and conspired against her. Did her son do th</span>
  <span id="freeText16456751081943995908" style="display:none">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I picked up Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Reading the synopsis really didn’t prepare me for how intense this book really is! I’m still not sure how to classify it, but I will say that I now have a better grasp of dark fiction as a genre... sub genre?<br /><br />The beginning has this hook- a woman’s nightmare - this violent crime against her spirals into a mother’s worst fear that her son has completely gone over the edge and conspired against her. Did her son do this horrible, unforgivable thing? She is refusing to believe it, but the evidence points right at him.<br /><br />Right when I begin to think I know where we are at in the book and am really getting prepped for the legal battle to find out if he’s guilty or innocent, the scene and tone of the whole book spins me inside out and now I’m on a mystic Seminole journey... and it gets intense but I hold on tight. There were times where I thought I was lost only to find myself again within the pages of The Speed of Life. Definitely an unforgettable read!!<br /></span>

<div id="review_2611069454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2611069454" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2611069454?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2611069454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11856232239358195428">‘His grandmomma taught him the ways of her Seminole and African ancestors— respect for the earth and his elders.’’<br/><br/>California author James Victor Jordan is a practicing attorney, having earned his JD from UCLA as well as a Master of Professional Writing degree from USC. He is a descendant of Eastern European shamans and writes fiction to explore justice, multiculturalism, spiritualism, and nature. His short stories have been widely published. He lives in Santa Monica, California. <br/><br/>Far too seldom d</span>
  <span id="freeText11856232239358195428" style="display:none">‘His grandmomma taught him the ways of her Seminole and African ancestors— respect for the earth and his elders.’’<br /><br />California author James Victor Jordan is a practicing attorney, having earned his JD from UCLA as well as a Master of Professional Writing degree from USC. He is a descendant of Eastern European shamans and writes fiction to explore justice, multiculturalism, spiritualism, and nature. His short stories have been widely published. He lives in Santa Monica, California. <br /><br />Far too seldom do we encounter debut novels the explore arenas of thought that stimulate our exploration of our own possibilities/potentials. James Victor Jordan is that rare persona who on his first outing in a full length novel finds aspects of story weaving that capture our attention on every page. In his brief bio he sates he is a descendant of shamans and for those who wonder, ‘a shaman is a person regarded as having access to, and influence in, the world of good and evil spirits, especially among some peoples of northern Asia and North America. Typically such people enter a trance state during a ritual, and practice divination and healing.’ Perhaps that is one major source of James’ inspiration. But there is far more to this mixture of adventure, court proceedings, existing shamans, the hormonal pitfalls of adolescence, confused tales of responsibility all tied together with superb art work – apparently from the hand of the author. It all works splendidly and breeds a need for more books from this fertile mind.<br /><br />The synopsis simplifies the complex story and provides a stimulus to curiosity to read the entire novel – ‘Estella Verus – part Seminole, part black, part white – a federal prosecutor in South Florida, is the victim of a home invasion during which she is beaten and raped. The perpetrator leaves a note saying that Estella’s son, Andrew, sent him to do it. When Andrew is charged with complicity in the crime, Estella is desperate to talk to him in her efforts to discover the truth, but while she’s still in the hospital recovering from her injuries, Andrew’s lawyer has her served with a restraining order, preventing her from talking to him to protect his Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination.’<br /><br />And as fascinating as the story is, the prose illuminates the world James has created: ‘Andrew’s going to the beach, looking good, shades covering his brown eyes, wearing his hair too short. On his way out the door, he says, “Be home before sundown, Momma.” He’s not allowed to drive at night. The latch clicks, and he’s gone. My balcony – my refuge when I weary from the demands of meting out justice – is cantilevered over a garden catching the light of the late-afternoon sun dancing and splashing over double hibiscus, second-bloom wisteria, and wild myrtle. I sip a lemon daiquiri. A fragrance of honeysuckle wafts in the air. A ruby-throated hummingbird flits from flower to flower to flower on a bottlebrush bush. In the rose beds, a golden rat snake crushes the last breath from a squealing young squirrel. A turkey vulture, majestic in flight, repulsive in sight, cawing, its fishhook-tipped talons extended like the fingers of an open hand, flaps its wings—spanning six feet—slowly, gracefully, as it descends to the upper fronds of a stately cabbage palmetto. Yesterday, when I cross-examined the defendant – formerly revered as “The Queen” by her elderly clients – her crown rested uneasy as she stammered, contradicted herself, and failed to reconcile her testimony with the story she’d told on direct. The incredulity of the jurors was palpable, an unmistakable harbinger of a loose swift sword. Her victims’ life savings were invested in a collapsed Ponzi scheme that paid for her chartered-jet excursions to Lake Como and ski vacations in Gstaad. The satisfaction of her victims with the judgment will be transitory, a brief respite from their anguish. But to turn the other cheek is to ignore moral imperative, and to disregard morality is to court extinction. This judge is fond of metaphor. A trial is a jigsaw puzzle, she told the jurors. Each piece of the puzzle is a piece of evidence. There is no order in which the pieces of the puzzle must be assembled. But you can’t see the puzzle’s entire picture until you have all the pieces. When all the evidence is presented, you will have all the pieces of the puzzle. Then following my instructions, it will be your job to put the puzzle together. You can only reach a proper decision after you’ve seen the entire picture.‘<br /><br />Only a few moments and we are pulled into this tale. Character development is superb, with each character growing in reality like a paining of a figure on a canvas. This is excellent writing from a man who has the gift. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11856232239358195428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3587469657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3587469657" />
    <a title="Carly Rheilan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97495424-carly-rheilan"><img alt="Carly Rheilan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584645110p2/97495424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3587469657?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carly Rheilan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carly Rheilan" href="/user/show/97495424-carly-rheilan">Carly Rheilan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3587469657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5931043919432572186">This is a unique and extraordinary book, cutting across mindsets as much as genres. <br/><br/>It can be read, just about, if you’re prepared to put the work in, as a crime thriller, a whodunit for the rape that slams through the early pages of this book. Sadly the violence and horror of that scene may make some readers stop there and decide the book is not for them, but press on if you can bear to, you will be repaid.<br/><br/>You may be better repaid if you think of it as a literary work, a meditation on conscious</span>
  <span id="freeText5931043919432572186" style="display:none">This is a unique and extraordinary book, cutting across mindsets as much as genres. <br /><br />It can be read, just about, if you’re prepared to put the work in, as a crime thriller, a whodunit for the rape that slams through the early pages of this book. Sadly the violence and horror of that scene may make some readers stop there and decide the book is not for them, but press on if you can bear to, you will be repaid.<br /><br />You may be better repaid if you think of it as a literary work, a meditation on consciousness and determinism. A physicist speculates about whether one could predict the future if one knew the trajectory of every object in space, every action and reaction in the infinite Newton’s cradle. A Seminole woman sees the future, as a child is born, locking into an inevitable prophesy. Throughout, the book traces the infinitely complex web of apparently unrelated actions and events, that underpin an eventual outcome. In the midst of such forces can anyone have free will?<br /><br />But to keep yourself from losing track, you might try to read it as a cultural saga – complex, spanning generations and timeframes and perspectives – a saga in which, no matter how the cultural backdrop changes, women hold the world together, and men – sons – disrupt it. Throughout this book, sons are problematic. <br /><br />But however you read it, you do have to put the work in. The intricacy of this work is intriguing, and the writing is sometimes quite mesmerising, but you can easily miss a step. It jumps in time and place and person, forwards and backwards. And the author does warn you. The process of the book is described rather neatly in a passage very near the beginning, in which a judge reflects on the nature of a trial: <i>A trial is a jigsaw puzzle, she told the jurors. Each piece of the puzzle is a piece of evidence. There is no order in which the pieces of the puzzle must be assembled. But you can’t see the puzzle’s entire picture until you have all the pieces. When all the evidence is presented, you will have all the pieces of the puzzle. Then following my instructions, it will be your job to put the puzzle together. You can only reach a proper decision after you’ve seen the entire picture.</i><br /><br />And it will, indeed, be your job, dear reader. The author gives instructions, and throws all the pieces of the puzzle into the mix. But you have to put it all together. Enjoy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5931043919432572186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11954519999783241557" style="display:none">Estella Verus – A whole Attorney in South Florida, but part seminole, black and white. Apart from being a professional she is also a mother. Andrew is her teenage son who is convicted for possession of substance.<br /><br />One night, Estella’a home is invaded and she is physically abused mercilessly. The perp has left a note to her stating that her son has sent him to her house. Apart from substance possession, Andrew is now charged with his. There are restraining orders and she feels hopeless.<br /><br />Thus begins the Speed of Life which has multiple plots and narrators.<br /><br />Is Andrew a real convict?<br />Is Estella going to prove her son’s innocence?<br />How do we know what is real and what is not?<br /><br />Rating – 4/5 Stars<br />Recommendation – High<br /><br />Conclusion,<br /><br />This thriller book is divided into seven parts, but the central plot is the mother’s quest for search of truth about her convicted son. Is it the truth or not is what Estella needs to ascertain. This read also gives us an Astrophysics angle and an exploration beyond law.<br /><br />Trigger Warning – Deals with physical abuse.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3577881051?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tori" href="/user/show/111771959-tori">Tori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3577881051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5375028847775316202">This book is a thriller, court drama, family drama as well as much more! <br/><br/>The novel is broken into seven parts which follows Estella Verus – part Seminole, part black, part white – who is a federal prosecutor in South Florida when she falls victim of a home invasion during which she is beaten and raped. The rapist leaves a note saying that Estella’s son, Andrew, sent him to do it. When Andrew is charged with complicity in the crime, Estella is desperate to talk to him in her efforts to discover t</span>
  <span id="freeText5375028847775316202" style="display:none">This book is a thriller, court drama, family drama as well as much more! <br /><br />The novel is broken into seven parts which follows Estella Verus – part Seminole, part black, part white – who is a federal prosecutor in South Florida when she falls victim of a home invasion during which she is beaten and raped. The rapist leaves a note saying that Estella’s son, Andrew, sent him to do it. When Andrew is charged with complicity in the crime, Estella is desperate to talk to him in her efforts to discover the truth, but while she’s still in the hospital recovering from her injuries, Andrew’s lawyer has her served with a restraining order, preventing her from talking to him to protect his Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination.<br /><br />The writing is extremely descriptive and you feel like you are in the exact locations they are describing. The description of the book was extremely intriguing for me, unfortunately the book itself was not something I would normally read. I struggled through parts of it, but overall it was a very good book. I would recommend to anyone who likes astrophysics and Shaman beliefs/stories.<br /><br />I received a free copy of the book from the publisher for a fair and honest review and all opinions are my own!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5375028847775316202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3489108658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3489108658" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22951160-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598732251p2/22951160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3489108658?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/22951160-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22951160-amanda?shelf=myths-legends">myths-legends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22951160-amanda?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22951160-amanda?shelf=americana">americana</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3489108658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6813883878039262010"><b>A thrilling journey of discovery</b><br/><br/>Federal prosecutor, Estella, is brutally raped. Her assailant claims her son, Andrew, put him up to it. Estella’s search for the truth uncovers a universe of potential realities.<br/><br/>The Speed of Life hits from the off with strong, dramatic action. Time warps and folds over itself in disorientating fashion. Once the reader acclimatises to the world of infinite possibilities, this is a thrilling ride. The atypical structure works well to highlight the novel’s many theme</span>
  <span id="freeText6813883878039262010" style="display:none"><b>A thrilling journey of discovery</b><br /><br />Federal prosecutor, Estella, is brutally raped. Her assailant claims her son, Andrew, put him up to it. Estella’s search for the truth uncovers a universe of potential realities.<br /><br />The Speed of Life hits from the off with strong, dramatic action. Time warps and folds over itself in disorientating fashion. Once the reader acclimatises to the world of infinite possibilities, this is a thrilling ride. The atypical structure works well to highlight the novel’s many themes and topics, including Seminole culture and history, astrophysics, metaphysics, philosophy, evolution, racism, myths, literature, the stories we tell ourselves…<br /><br />The novel has a lively and substantial cast, all well-characterised, although their relationship to each other might have been clearer, particularly where a character has been off in the wings for one part of the book. The narration is from several points of view, and in the transition to the next POV, it is not always clear whose eyes we are looking through. But, if there are uncertainties, it adds to the sense of questing for the truth.<br /><br />Jordan strikes a fine balance between intense drama and the internal world of his characters. In the main, his prose is sharp with a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1377.Raymond_Chandler" title="Raymond Chandler" rel="nofollow noopener">Raymond Chandler</a>-esque hardboiled wit. He uses his experience as an attorney to great effect in the legal terminology and courtroom scene.<br /><br />The way the author covers such a wide range of ideas over the course of the book is reminiscent of the best of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/197.Tom_Robbins" title="Tom Robbins" rel="nofollow noopener">Tom Robbins</a>. The philosophical and space-time aspects will appeal to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93436.The_End_of_Mr__Y" title="The End of Mr. Y by Scarlett Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The End of Mr. Y</a> by Scarlett Thomas.<br /><br />The illustrations are a collaboration between the author and Eric Savage (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.savagecreative.com">www.savagecreative.com</a>), plus Loraine Hall.<br /><br />A remarkable debut.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6813883878039262010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2694136279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694136279" />
    <a title="Library Love" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74893905-library-love"><img alt="Library Love" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513106838p2/74893905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694136279?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Library Love" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Library Love" href="/user/show/74893905-library-love">Library Love</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694136279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4126323794571842825">Jordan starts this novel with the character Estella, a mixed race judge with a 20-year-old son, who is on probation. Estella becomes the victim of a brutal rape (and Jordan does not shy away from gritty detail in this well-written, tense scene). Readers are therefore provided with different perspectives on crime to consider, that of the judge, the family of a perpetrator and the victim. <br/><br/>The story is told in the form of multiple vignettes, all rich in detail. Readers should be prepared for a lot </span>
  <span id="freeText4126323794571842825" style="display:none">Jordan starts this novel with the character Estella, a mixed race judge with a 20-year-old son, who is on probation. Estella becomes the victim of a brutal rape (and Jordan does not shy away from gritty detail in this well-written, tense scene). Readers are therefore provided with different perspectives on crime to consider, that of the judge, the family of a perpetrator and the victim. <br /><br />The story is told in the form of multiple vignettes, all rich in detail. Readers should be prepared for a lot of deaths (there is a pretty high body count in this story) but balanced with sprinklings of almost painterly, poetic descriptions throughout. <br /><br />This is partly unfolding courtroom drama, partly the woven together histories of the characters, and all via a journey taking in eclectic aspects including metaphysics, quantum mechanics, religion, consciousness, astronomy and history. All in all this is quite a page-turner!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4126323794571842825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1428331590614643732">The Speed of Life: An Illustrated Novel by James Victor Jordan is a heady mix of genres in one book. You have a thriller, physics and even spirituality. The book opens with a brutal rape of Estella and from there the story kind of jumps around as chapters veer from one character to another. Even with these disparate elements though, the plot evolves and everything begins to come together and finally make sense. It is a journey to come to the resolution in the book. The surroundings in Florida ar</span>
  <span id="freeText1428331590614643732" style="display:none">The Speed of Life: An Illustrated Novel by James Victor Jordan is a heady mix of genres in one book. You have a thriller, physics and even spirituality. The book opens with a brutal rape of Estella and from there the story kind of jumps around as chapters veer from one character to another. Even with these disparate elements though, the plot evolves and everything begins to come together and finally make sense. It is a journey to come to the resolution in the book. The surroundings in Florida are accurately described, as one feels the humidity, explores the fauna, and even the slimy creatures that abound. Seminole culture and mythology are also explored, lending credence to the backdrop of the plot. Highly recommend for an entirely different kind of reading experience. The author has come up with something here that is completely unique and riveting. </span>

  <span id="freeText11802596311706188608" style="display:none">Don't you just love it when you discover a novel that is completely unique, different from what you have ever read before? 'The Speed of Life' by James Victor Jordan sets itself apart from other thriller novels, but using an interesting structure and wide range of characters, ranging from a physicist, Native American, philosopher, amongst others, all of which are connected to the grizzly attack on a lawyer. You learn so much from the characters as you journey from the battle in the courtroom to the ancient tales of the Everglades.<br /><br />A beautifully written piece of contemporary fiction, which manages to weave in seemingly disparate themes such as courtroom politics, mythology, family relationships, and even theoretical physics, to create a plot that is engaging, extraordinary, and unique. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11594992150756386616">I struggle to define The Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Yes it is essentially a fast-paced thriller, investigating a brutal crime, but it is also so much more. A diverse cast of characters introduce Western philosophy, astrophysics, human nature, and American Mythology, for a rich and multi-faceted plot that it gripping and thought-provoking. Several storylines wind around one another and come together for a thrilling conclusion that will leave you wanting more from Jordan. Through The Sp</span>
  <span id="freeText11594992150756386616" style="display:none">I struggle to define The Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Yes it is essentially a fast-paced thriller, investigating a brutal crime, but it is also so much more. A diverse cast of characters introduce Western philosophy, astrophysics, human nature, and American Mythology, for a rich and multi-faceted plot that it gripping and thought-provoking. Several storylines wind around one another and come together for a thrilling conclusion that will leave you wanting more from Jordan. Through The Speed of Life, I felt that I learned a lot about the human spirit, and how it is the relationships between one another can be so strong, yet so fragile. An excellent read that I know will stay with me for a long time.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3593652212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3593652212" />
    <a title="Rowena Andrews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100423082-rowena-andrews"><img alt="Rowena Andrews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564087415p2/100423082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3593652212?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rowena Andrews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rowena Andrews" href="/user/show/100423082-rowena-andrews">Rowena Andrews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/44003572-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3593652212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9290230949715569954">This was a difficult review to write, in part because The Speed of Life is a difficult book to define as it is a novel that touches on many different aspects. However, at its heart, it is a legal thriller about a crime and everything that spirals around that, from what lead to that moment, to the aftermath and fallout. It is also, unfortunately, a book that I struggled to connect with, something which is certainly more personal than anything else, because this is a beautiful book. The writing is</span>
  <span id="freeText9290230949715569954" style="display:none">This was a difficult review to write, in part because The Speed of Life is a difficult book to define as it is a novel that touches on many different aspects. However, at its heart, it is a legal thriller about a crime and everything that spirals around that, from what lead to that moment, to the aftermath and fallout. It is also, unfortunately, a book that I struggled to connect with, something which is certainly more personal than anything else, because this is a beautiful book. The writing is fantastic, with some genuinely stunning descriptions paired with the illustrations done in with Eric Savage and Lorraine Hall.<br />“After all, what is consciousness if not a dialog between the past, the present, and the future? What are memories and dreams if not an expression of the speed of life?”<br /> This quote is quite an apt representation of what this book is, and there was a dreamlike quality to the book which kept me reading to the end, even with my own complicated feelings about the book. The Speed of Life is one of those books that grabs hold of you, and makes you think about far more than just the clever, twisting crime story in the centre, but about questions of family and justice, past and present. It is a brilliant, multi-layered story, and I can see why many people have loved it.<br /> I think perhaps for me the disconnect came through the characters, because this is a fast-paced story, with multiple povs and time jumps. Which has the potential to make for a very confusing story, but in this case is woven together to make a coherent story that moves back and forth through time. However, it did feel as though as I was never able to truly make a connection with the characters, and with the jumps, you couldn’t take your eyes off the page long enough to make sense of what you did have because otherwise, you would lose the flow or an essential thread of the story. That said, I did feel that each of the pov characters had a strong, individual voice, and you could always tell who you were following.<br /> This is not an easy read, with a brutal crime (tw: rape) and a complicated, interweaving of povs and timelines. Still, I would recommend for anyone who wants something different from your usual crime thriller—a beautiful book, a strong debut, and one that many will fall in love with.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9290230949715569954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3588199193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3588199193" />
    <a title="Dark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122298395-dark"><img alt="Dark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601586392p2/122298395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3588199193?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark" href="/user/show/122298395-dark">Dark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3588199193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13200670321864331540">Reading this mysterious book, I kept thinking of those elaborate monkey’s paw knots that my dad, an old naval man, used to make for me. As a child I would hold the huge knot in one hand, like a talisman, and with the other trace the cords round and round, trying to see how the different threads wove in, wove out, getting lost in the mystery of it… This book was like that.<br/><br/>I read a lot of crime books, and there’s a crime story here (that thread at least I managed to untangle by the end, to see how</span>
  <span id="freeText13200670321864331540" style="display:none">Reading this mysterious book, I kept thinking of those elaborate monkey’s paw knots that my dad, an old naval man, used to make for me. As a child I would hold the huge knot in one hand, like a talisman, and with the other trace the cords round and round, trying to see how the different threads wove in, wove out, getting lost in the mystery of it… This book was like that.<br /><br />I read a lot of crime books, and there’s a crime story here (that thread at least I managed to untangle by the end, to see how it fitted into the knot – I’d have been unhappy if I hadn’t managed that). And it’s a good crime story – at first it looks like a unitary one, a terrible crime against a female victim – but the mystery of that crime dives rapidly underground burrowing through the story and transforming into a mystery of other crimes, further, wider, money, diamonds, revenge… I liked that. I’d have been satisfied with that, on its own. <br /><br />But inside the crime story there’s also a magical realist story about a family, transitioning across the generations from a shamanistic, native American past, into the current 'scientific' world. Both worlds are presented as equally magical, violent and troubling, and a thread of a story about astrophysics links them. The magical purple light that is invariably a signifier of the violence of the shamanistic world – most shockingly and yet never really interrogated, the murder of a baby – seems to be echoed in the photons of black holes, disclosing terrible secrets about ontold crimes in modernity. I never did completely untangle those threads, though I tried…<br /><br />By preference I’m a left brain thinker: I like to take things apart and unpick their logic, and in another book I might have minded more that I couldn’t always do this. But the beautiful illustrations are important here: they speak to the right of your brain, and they bind the narratives together in ways that you understand differently. I’ve never seen pictures used like that in an adult book of fiction. It worked for me.<br /><br />This isn’t a book you can read in one sitting, but it’s also not a book to pick up and put down in snatched moments between other things. It needs its own time. Maybe it’s a good book to read while you’re locked down or quarantined – some point in your life when you can focus on the interwoven narratives and forget about everything else. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13200670321864331540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="De Gevallene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="De Gevallene" href="/user/show/106883708-de-gevallene">De Gevallene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592891722" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16279770099335501236">I’m glad that I’m sufficiently bloody minded that having got such a bargain (paying just .99c for a kindle of this beautiful book!) I was determined to finish it even though it annoyed me quite a lot from the start: it triggered a whole raft of my "irritation buttons". <br/><br/>All the same, I could not escape the observation that it’s an impressively good book.<br/><br/>Don't try to skim it - you'll get completely lost in the changes of scene and person and timeline. <br/><br/>Give it time, and what you will find is an exq</span>
  <span id="freeText16279770099335501236" style="display:none">I’m glad that I’m sufficiently bloody minded that having got such a bargain (paying just .99c for a kindle of this beautiful book!) I was determined to finish it even though it annoyed me quite a lot from the start: it triggered a whole raft of my "irritation buttons". <br /><br />All the same, I could not escape the observation that it’s an impressively good book.<br /><br />Don't try to skim it - you'll get completely lost in the changes of scene and person and timeline. <br /><br />Give it time, and what you will find is an exquisite exploration of the interconnectedness of human experience, beneath the invisible surface of everything – our lives endlessly bound up with those of strangers. And a thoughtful, open-minded writer, intelligently exploring questions about free will, about the possibility of relationship if there is no free will, about consciousness, about where we have come from, where we are going. All the while building a clever crime story to a deeply satisfying denouement.<br /><br />Throughout this is a project of elusive fragility – through the beautiful, mystifyingly connected illustrations that punctuate each part of the book, through snatches of dialogue, through scenes that seem out of place, out of time. It is a book written as dreams are written – tangential, familiar, strange. A question from the book, that I copied down as I read it: <i>“After all, what is consciousness if not a dialog between the past, the present, and the future? What are memories and dreams if not an expression of the speed of life?”</i><br /><br />At that moment I was awe struck. I knew I loved this book.<br /><br />It was a tough weekend though, with this book pinning me down and making me read every word. Later I might decide that I had Stockholm Syndrome. In that case I’ll have to make do with being happy that I read the book before my friends did, since I rather predict that it’s heading for a Booker Prize. (Even if it’s only short listed, I’ll be one up on anyone who tries to bluff about it from the gush on Twitter. I hope my friends will be impressed.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16279770099335501236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3596980979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5748791344576992293">4 Stars<br/><br/>When this book was recommended to me recently, I was quite intrigued by the title and cover- but to be honest, I really wasn’t sure whether I would enjoy it. But, my curiosity got the better of me and my trigger finger took action by one-clicking a copy to explore. I am so happy I took a chance on this book as I enjoyed every minute between the covers.<br/>The Speed of Life: An illustrated Novel is the debut book by James Victor Jordan. If you are like me and wondered about the ‘illustrated’ p</span>
  <span id="freeText5748791344576992293" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />When this book was recommended to me recently, I was quite intrigued by the title and cover- but to be honest, I really wasn’t sure whether I would enjoy it. But, my curiosity got the better of me and my trigger finger took action by one-clicking a copy to explore. I am so happy I took a chance on this book as I enjoyed every minute between the covers.<br />The Speed of Life: An illustrated Novel is the debut book by James Victor Jordan. If you are like me and wondered about the ‘illustrated’ part of the title, don’t worry, this isn’t like a picture book- but it does have several illustrations sprinkled though the story. I felt that the pictures helped to set the tone and mood of the story- whist adding a little intrigue.<br />This is one of those books that I really don’t know how to categorise- or explain it well enough to do it the justice that it deserves. The Speed of Life has so much going on in it, but in a good way. The book is quite a rich and vivid tapestry that encompasses so many different elements- and is a clever, smart, engaging, and multi-faceted feast of a story. <br />From Seminole culture and mythology, Shamanic practices, spirituality, and philosophy- the author pulls us into a tale of courage, cruelty, secrets, hope, drama, thrilling developments, intrigue, action and balancing it all with plenty of emotion. There was so much to wrap my mind around- it really is a thought provoking story- even now as I am writing this review, loooong after closing the book, my mind is still pondering the dynamic story the author created.<br />I won’t go into any detail as I really don’t want to spoil it for you- your really should grab a copy and discover all the intriguing details for yourself.<br />Well worth the read!<br /><br />Thank you, James Victor Jordan.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5748791344576992293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3589535163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3589535163" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3589535163?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anastasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anastasia" href="/user/show/115601704-anastasia">Anastasia</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3589535163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16426960050845969242">I just did not get this book. I’m not the kind of girl who lets people down, and I promised Blackthorn Book Tours I would read it. But I just did not get it.<br/><br/>So many characters, so much jumping around! Where am I? Who is this? Have I met them before? What are they doing in this story? What year is it supposed to be now? The characters flit in and there are an awful lot of them, some who appear only once, in intense detail (though I couldn’t always see why they were included) and others who kept r</span>
  <span id="freeText16426960050845969242" style="display:none">I just did not get this book. I’m not the kind of girl who lets people down, and I promised Blackthorn Book Tours I would read it. But I just did not get it.<br /><br />So many characters, so much jumping around! Where am I? Who is this? Have I met them before? What are they doing in this story? What year is it supposed to be now? The characters flit in and there are an awful lot of them, some who appear only once, in intense detail (though I couldn’t always see why they were included) and others who kept resurfacing, perhaps ten years younger or twenty older than the last time I met them, in scenes whose significance I couldn’t fathom.<br />I wished that the author had included a duffers’ guide listing all the characters, with a sentence of aide memoire about each. But judging from the VIPs whose reviews are quoted at the beginning, I don’t think he was writing for duffers...<br /><br />So I’m not going to award stars to this book, because I don’t think it’s for me to do so. <br />I just want to give it a shout out for two reasons.<br /><br />First for the beautiful descriptions of the natural world – I really enjoyed these, and I didn’t care how they fitted in the story. At moments I was transported quite out of myself and into the Everglades. In color. Nice. Thank you for that Mr Jordan. <br /><br />Second for the amazing pictures – also in colour - beautiful, funny and mysterious. I spent half an hour the other day, taking a break, just looking at each of them and thinking how delicious it would be to do them as tattoos. On the author, maybe. I quite got into that reverie. Thank you for that, artists ERIC SAVAGE <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://savagecreative.com/">https://savagecreative.com/</a> and LORRAINE HALL. (I put the artists’ name in capitals because although the book trumpets itself as ‘an illustrated novel’ so the pictures are presumably important, the author does not seem keen to share his limelight, and the illustrators’ names are as hidden as can legally be got away with. The author hasn’t even included them in his acknowledgements!) <br /><br />Didn’t get it, sorry, but I hope you do. And even without getting it, I got some pleasure from it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16426960050845969242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11362026902585743689">What are memories and dreams if not an expression of the speed of life.”<br/>This book has lots of complex layers so be ready!<br/>It feels at first like there are several stories going on in this book but just be patient and you will see how everything connects.<br/>The book is mostly set in South Florida and intertwines a horrific rape with the metaphysical world, shamanism, and old high school friends that are interconnected through love and deceit.<br/>The book begins with Estella’s, an attorney, sustains a bru</span>
  <span id="freeText11362026902585743689" style="display:none">What are memories and dreams if not an expression of the speed of life.”<br />This book has lots of complex layers so be ready!<br />It feels at first like there are several stories going on in this book but just be patient and you will see how everything connects.<br />The book is mostly set in South Florida and intertwines a horrific rape with the metaphysical world, shamanism, and old high school friends that are interconnected through love and deceit.<br />The book begins with Estella’s, an attorney, sustains a brutal attack and her son, Andrew, is arrested as having set his mother up for the attack. We then move to an interesting history of Estella’s past and her family. The book then become almost for me a legal thriller as old high school friends are involved in one way or another in an accused money laundering scheme.<br />I think it’s important to focus on the chapter about the characters when they are in high school because those characters are integral to the story. <br />There is also a portion of the story that takes place in California and focuses on Georges. This part delves into the Sudan and Jewish culture and hate. Abe, a 24 year old, takes part in this section and it’s very powerful and interesting.<br />When you read this book, the details are important so don’t overlook them. My impression of the characters are for the most part that everyone in this story has high levels of education which I think should be recognized.<br />There are beautiful illustrations throughout the book. <br />An interesting and thought provoking novel!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3591834077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11283403830104260568">The novel begins with James Victor Jordan shocking the reader shortly after introducing the first of his central protagonists, Estella, who in the early pages of the novel is the victim of a brutal and violent rape. The novel then continues in seven separate parts, featuring seven different character groups, all connected, although it is not immediately apparent how.<br/><br/>The key themes in the novel are of love, identity, fate, guilt, and deceit. I will also add trigger warnings of violence, rape, rac</span>
  <span id="freeText11283403830104260568" style="display:none">The novel begins with James Victor Jordan shocking the reader shortly after introducing the first of his central protagonists, Estella, who in the early pages of the novel is the victim of a brutal and violent rape. The novel then continues in seven separate parts, featuring seven different character groups, all connected, although it is not immediately apparent how.<br /><br />The key themes in the novel are of love, identity, fate, guilt, and deceit. I will also add trigger warnings of violence, rape, racial and sexual prejudice, drug abuse and coping with trauma.<br /><br />The plot itself had great potential, and James Victor Jordan takes the time to develop each group of characters, and engage the reader in their world. However, I must admit whilst I enjoyed the spiritual and philosophical references, I struggled to follow the frequent, lengthy and detailed meanderings which I felt detracted from, rather than enhancing the plot.<br /><br />My personal view was that there was far too much crammed into this novel and it became a little overwhelming; lengthy philosophical and spiritual reflections, multiple separate parts and subplots that each could have been ideas for separate novels, and several strong protagonists each with tangential character arcs that could have easily been developed further.<br /><br />I was originally intrigued by the concept of this being labelled as an ‘illustrated novel’, but, personally, was disappointed, and felt there were too few, as I think I counted only 7 in c300 pages.<br /><br />I would like to thank Blackthorntours for an e-copy of this novel and inviting me to share my honest review as part of The Speed of Life book tour.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11283403830104260568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3592292664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3592292664" />
    <a title="Linda McCutcheon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28194465-linda-mccutcheon"><img alt="Linda McCutcheon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3592292664?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda McCutcheon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda McCutcheon" href="/user/show/28194465-linda-mccutcheon">Linda McCutcheon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781732514300" href="/book/show/43693011-the-speed-of-life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592292664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17782351591203575853">The Speed of Life: An Illustrated Novel by James Victor Jordan is truly like no other novel I have experienced in my life. It is part thriller, court drama, family drama with some theoretical astrophysics and Shaman beliefs thrown into the mix.<br/><br/>Broken into seven parts the central story is heartbreakingly about federal prosecutor Estella who is the victim of an horrendous home invasion where she is brutally beaten and raped by her assailant. He leaves a note at the crime scene that her son Andrew </span>
  <span id="freeText17782351591203575853" style="display:none">The Speed of Life: An Illustrated Novel by James Victor Jordan is truly like no other novel I have experienced in my life. It is part thriller, court drama, family drama with some theoretical astrophysics and Shaman beliefs thrown into the mix.<br /><br />Broken into seven parts the central story is heartbreakingly about federal prosecutor Estella who is the victim of an horrendous home invasion where she is brutally beaten and raped by her assailant. He leaves a note at the crime scene that her son Andrew sent him to commit this unspeakable crime. Andrew is arrested and Estella cannot even speak to him because his lawyer has issued a restraining order against her to protect his rights. She needs to hear the truth from him but will have to put the pieces together herself on how and why her and her son ended up in this living nightmare.<br /><br />Just this premise would be enough for me to read this book but the author remarkably manages to apply laws of astrophysics and mysticism to demonstrate the human journey through life's pains and joys.<br /><br />The writing is so precise and descriptive but yet there is almost a lyrical tone to it. I admit that I was confused at times and had to re read passages and look up definitions now and then but I would not have wanted to miss the experience of all this story has to offer not just as a thriller but as a lesson on the connectivity we all have to one another.<br /><br />I received a free copy of this book from the publisher for a fair and honest review. All opinions are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17782351591203575853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer10770157484807073661">4/5 Stars! Full review is on my blog: <a href='https://anoveldestination.com/the-speed-of-life/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Speed of Life Review</a><br/><br/>Content Warning: This book deals with rape and violence, including some graphic descriptions.<br/><br/>I was provided a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. It has the traditional plot elements needed to keep a reader intrigued: mystery, suspense, and solid pacing. However, the movement of the story also felt original. I enjoyed how the book jumps between times, places, and people. I like the different </span>
  <span id="freeText10770157484807073661" style="display:none">4/5 Stars! Full review is on my blog: <a href="https://anoveldestination.com/the-speed-of-life/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Speed of Life Review</a><br /><br />Content Warning: This book deals with rape and violence, including some graphic descriptions.<br /><br />I was provided a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It has the traditional plot elements needed to keep a reader intrigued: mystery, suspense, and solid pacing. However, the movement of the story also felt original. I enjoyed how the book jumps between times, places, and people. I like the different perspectives, and there was one single thread running throughout that kept the story coherent.<br /><br />Another thing I enjoyed in this book was the setting, specifically the descriptions of the Everglades. Beyond setting, I also liked how this book incorporated shamanism and Seminole culture. In general, while this book deals with some heavier topics, I think the themes were handled well.<br /><br />My only critique is that sometimes the book goes on long digressions to discuss the different topics/themes in the book. For me, these digressions detracted from the solid story and plot in the book. Still, the writing style overall was enjoyable, and there are some genuinely beautiful sentences that I reread several times. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10486425494772691310">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I picked up Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Reading the synopsis really didn’t prepare me for how intense this book really is! I’m still not sure how to classify it, but I will say that I now have a better grasp of dark fiction as a genre... sub genre?<br/><br/>The beginning has this hook- a woman’s nightmare - this violent crime against her spirals into a mother’s worst fear that her son has completely gone over the edge and conspired against her. Did her son do th</span>
  <span id="freeText10486425494772691310" style="display:none">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I picked up Speed of Life by James Victor Jordan. Reading the synopsis really didn’t prepare me for how intense this book really is! I’m still not sure how to classify it, but I will say that I now have a better grasp of dark fiction as a genre... sub genre?<br /><br />The beginning has this hook- a woman’s nightmare - this violent crime against her spirals into a mother’s worst fear that her son has completely gone over the edge and conspired against her. Did her son do this horrible, unforgivable thing? She is refusing to believe it, but the evidence points right at him.<br /><br />Right when I begin to think I know where we are at in the book and am really getting prepped for the legal battle to find out if he’s guilty or innocent, the scene and tone of the whole book spins me inside out and now I’m on a mystic Seminole journey... and it gets intense but I hold on tight. There were times where I thought I was lost only to find myself again within the pages of The Speed of Life. Definitely an unforgettable read!!<br /></span>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aeVysgDWLcV0A2VnKSKq2m+xc53BFf3b1MkWWFGuoarQyDXJ/LfuxVEAbbWvOVON+o4Vyrt6Kc/4H4mGaCWq2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Gjk9PDdzMg+Bw2+tLW4JXll04c3kIrxIoQ6kPv0A6FujFHpHyxLxD6TAZ3+rdfAJzEuHmp5NaFyN2DvgxIvjKQ==')})
  }

The book is scheduled for release on the 1st of October. As a Business Strategy and Psychological Warfare Consultant, M.D. White wrote this book utilizing his countless experiences over the years to properly proffer working, tested and trusted strategies to help business owners or employees, business managers or executives, politicians and or public figures manage high-stake business and leadership situations with the greatest success. White had this to say: &quot;No amount of experience in crucial conversations, or business negotiations, can prepare you better than the information you\'ll gleam from this manual. It\'s truly a politician’s guide to psychological warfare. Perhaps its President Trumps bible, and what he reads everynight. The moral of the story is: Use it, or be used by it! Current geopolitical controversies only emphasize this point.&quot; Many have deliberated over the effect of military strategies in business, but M.D. White cuts to the chase and reveals the raw and missing pieces all other military strategy discussions have left out. In this book, White extracts the key ingredients of military strategies and the applications which are left out in most discussions. For the first time ever there is a clear work-around of military strategies and an easy to understand roadmap on learning how to unlock, grow and strengthen from within one’s influence, presence and abilities. The Author further stressed the effectiveness of military strategies in business. “This military-based guide to business takes the best wartime tactics and practices and teaches you how you can apply them in your business—and your political or personal life—successfully. Developed within a systematic and comprehensive framework, this book utilizes the art of war in a whole new way and reveals that the path to a smooth business victory and mutually beneficial dialogue can be found in an unexpected but rewarding place.”  The world of business is a battlefield. You must be prepared.  Sun Tzu said, “The art of war teaches us to rely not on the likelihood of the enemy’s not coming, but on our own readiness to receive him.” The takeaway? Do everything in your power to be prepared, because it\'s only a matter of time before something goes wrong. If you are running, founding, working in any business, or are in an environment where ‘politics’ yield to nobody, The Influence of Military Strategies to Business is the preparation you need to succeed.  This military-based guide to business takes the best wartime tactics and practices and teaches you how you can apply them in your business—and your personal life—successfully. <span id="freeTextContainer17658831765802155880">James Victor Jordan, a descendant of Eastern European shamans, writes fiction to explore justice, multiculturalism, spiritualism, and nature. His short stories have been widely published. He is an attorney holding a JD degree from UCLA and a Master of Professional Writing degree from the University of Southern California. He lives in Santa Monica, California with his best friends: Andrea, his wife</span>
  <span id="freeText17658831765802155880" style="display:none">James Victor Jordan, a descendant of Eastern European shamans, writes fiction to explore justice, multiculturalism, spiritualism, and nature. His short stories have been widely published. He is an attorney holding a JD degree from UCLA and a Master of Professional Writing degree from the University of Southern California. He lives in Santa Monica, California with his best friends: Andrea, his wife and UC, their standard poodle. </span>
